      class=\"inline-share-btn inline-share-btn-more\"\n         data-share-method=\"facebook\"\n         data-uotrack=\"InlineShareMoreBtn\"><span class=\"inline-share-count inline-share-count-more\"></span><span class=\"inline-share-btn-label inline-share-btn-label-more\">MORE</span></span></div></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>The woman isn't identified. She's yelling. There's noise in the background.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>It's seconds after 20\u00a0shots, possibly more, were fired inside Cameo nightclub where she was with friends on Sunday morning. She calls 911.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><em>\"There is blood everywhere. He may not make it. Hurry up! Please. He\u00a0got blood all over his body. There shouldn't be shooting at clubs. We was all just dancing, next thing you look around he's shot. Friends pick up and put him in a car... damn I don't really expect anyone to get (expletive) shot in a club.\"</em></p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>It's one of 11 calls pleading for emergency assistance.<em>\u00a0</em>Some are calm. Some carry the same theme of begging emergency workers to hurry. Some simply report there was a shooting.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Cincinnati police released documents and audio files Wednesday pertaining to Sunday's Cameo nightclub shooting where 17 people were shot, one fatally.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>An incident report\u00a0showed the victims were 14 men and three women. They range in age from 24 to 33.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>O'Bryan Spikes, 27, died at the scene from a single shot to the chest, according to the Hamilton County Coroner's Office.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-P1i5_H-EsWE\" class=\"story-asset gallery-asset\"><div class=\"card-film inactive\"></div><div class=\"sidebar-gallery-btn cxenseparse_start --><p>The injured: Rodney Espy, 30, Deondre Davis, 29, Jraejah Warren, 28, Stephen Haley, 28, Rayshunda Higgins, 33, Jarrod Givens, 26, Ronald Lee, 33, Nathan McClendon, 27, Shannon Brown, 25, Jordan Harris, 24, Valor Stanley, 28, Bryant Stevenson, 28, Christopher Harris, 33, Michael Feagins Jr., 30, Khristian Howell, 25 and Regina Madaris, 33.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Of the 16 survivors, all but two have been released from area hospitals. The two that remain are in <a href=\"/story/news/2017/03/27/inside-ucs-trauma-center-during-cameo-shooting/99671050/\">critical condition at University of Cincinnati Medical Center</a>.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Sixty-nine law enforcement and fire personnel responded to the Cameo scene, which began unfolding around 1:30 a.m., records show.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Officers at the scene shouted to dispatchers, \"Everything you got! Expedite. Right now! Get me cars now!\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>District 4 Fire Chief Marc Monahan, who coordinated the chaotic scene, <a href=\"/story/news/2017/03/28/sorting-through-cameo-chaos-district-4-fire-chief-has-job-do/99707282/\">told The Enquirer earlier this week</a> the call came in that six to 10 people had been shot. It would turn out to be the worst mass shooting in the city's history.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-P1i5_H-sPvc\" class=\"story-asset oembed-asset\"><div class=\"story-oembed-wrap \"><div \n        class=\"js-oembed story-oembed story-oembed-cincinnaticom story-oembed-type-link\"\n        data-oembed-type=\"link\"\n        data-oembed-provider=\"cincinnaticom\"><style>\n    .oembed-asset-link { border-bottom: 1px solid #e1e1e1; }\n    .oembed-link-anchor { display: block; clear: both; }\n    p.oembed-link-desc { font-size: 100%; color: #666; font-weight: normal; margin: 0 14px 14px 14px; font-family: 'Futura Today Light'; text-align: left; line-height: 120%; }\n</style><div class=\"oembed-asset oembed-asset-link oembed-asset-cincinnati.com oembed-simple-link-container\"><a href=\"http://www.cincinnati.com/story/news/2017/03/28/pastor-obryan-spikes-many-people-liked-him-if-not-they-loved-him/99731674/\" data-track-label=\"newrecircinline\" class=\"oembed-simple-link oembed-link-anchor\"><p class=\"oembed-link-desc\">Pastor of O&#39;Bryan Spikes: &#39;Many people liked him if not, they loved him&#39;</p><div style=\"clear: both;\"></div></a></div></div></div></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>The initial call came in at 1:29\u00a0a.m. The club stayed open until 4 a.m. Police accounts say a couple of hundred people were inside at the time.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>People jumped out windows and ditched shoes, perfume and phones in the parking lot so they could move faster or hide in the bathroom, too far from the door. Some people suffered injuries while fleeing, trampled in the madness.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>By 1:31 a.m. police at the scene reported \"at least six victims.\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>At 1:45 a.m., two\u00a0officers reported to dispatchers that they detained someone who was standing in the club with a gun.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>At 2:12 a.m., an officer reported to a\u00a0dispatcher that a gun was recovered.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-P1i5_H-g0tc\" class=\"story-asset oembed-asset\"><div class=\"story-oembed-wrap \"><div \n        class=\"js-oembed story-oembed story-oembed-cincinnaticom story-oembed-type-link\"\n        data-oembed-type=\"link\"\n        data-oembed-provider=\"cincinnaticom\"><style>\n    .oembed-asset-link { border-bottom: 1px solid #e1e1e1; }\n    .oembed-link-anchor { display: block; clear: both; }\n    p.oembed-link-desc { font-size: 100%; color: #666; font-weight: normal; margin: 0 14px 14px 14px; font-family: 'Futura Today Light'; text-align: left; line-height: 120%; }\n</style><div class=\"oembed-asset oembed-asset-link oembed-asset-cincinnati.com oembed-simple-link-container\"><a href=\"http://www.cincinnati.com/story/news/2017/03/28/logs-shed-light-police-calls-cameo-nightclub/99728580/\" data-track-label=\"newrecircinline\" class=\"oembed-simple-link oembed-link-anchor\"><p class=\"oembed-link-desc\">Police called frequently to nightclub site</p><div style=\"clear: both;\"></div></a></div></div></div></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>There have been no arrests. Police Chief Eliot Isaac said Monday he is confident police will find the people responsible for this.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>In one 911 call, a caller tells the dispatcher, \"My friend's been shot. Hurry up! Hurry up!\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>The dispatcher asks if the caller knows who shot his friend and the caller replies no. The caller can be heard asking someone if they should load the shooting victim into a vehicle.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\"Do not move him. Hello? Please do not move him,\" the dispatcher says.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Another caller tells a dispatcher he has two friends shot.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\"I was running for my life,\" the caller said after being asked if he saw anything.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Another person called from the bathroom.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\"I'm in the bathroom and they're saying they're shooting inside and outside. And I don't know what to do, I lost my friend.\" Later, the caller asks the dispatcher, \"Is it done?\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-P1i5_H_areU\" class=\"story-asset cxenseparse_start --><p>Eight minutes after the initial dispatch call, a dispatcher reported, \"Any available unit in the city is responding at this time, plus county units.\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Officers on the scene were finding people in cars and down the road. They had been shot but fled.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>One man was found shot under the entrance awning. Two others in a car. One man who had been shot in the head was picked up by an\u00a0ambulance at\u00a0near Stanley Avenue.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Twelve minutes after the initial dispatch another victim was located in the nightclub's parking lot.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Some victims drove themselves to the hospital.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-P1i5_H-xNXI\" class=\"story-asset oembed-asset\"><div class=\"story-oembed-wrap \"><div \n        class=\"js-oembed story-oembed story-oembed-cincinnaticom story-oembed-type-link\"\n        data-oembed-type=\"link\"\n        data-oembed-provider=\"cincinnaticom\"><style>\n    .oembed-asset-link { border-bottom: 1px solid #e1e1e1; }\n    .oembed-link-anchor { display: block; clear: both; }\n    p.oembed-link-desc { font-size: 100%; color: #666; font-weight: normal; margin: 0 14px 14px 14px; font-family: 'Futura Today Light'; text-align: left; line-height: 120%; }\n</style><div class=\"oembed-asset oembed-asset-link oembed-asset-cincinnati.com oembed-simple-link-container\"><a href=\"http://www.cincinnati.com/story/news/crime/2017/03/29/timeline-response-police-radio-traffic-cameo-mass-shooting/99802920/\" data-track-label=\"newrecircinline\" class=\"oembed-simple-link oembed-link-anchor\"><p class=\"oembed-link-desc\">Timeline response: Police radio traffic from the Cameo mass shooting</p><div style=\"clear: both;\"></div></a></div></div></div></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>According to dispatch traffic, by 1:49 a.m. two shooting victims had walked into University of Cincinnati Medical Center. Twenty minutes later two \"walk-in\" shooting victims arrived at Bethesda North Hospital.\u00a0More than 45 minutes after the initial call, another victim walked into the Short Vine fire station.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Cincinnati City Manager Harry Black told city council Wednesday that police officers investigating the Cameo\u00a0nightclub\u00a0shootings are \"making substantial and significant progress.\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>But, he urged patience.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\"There are a lot of\u00a0witnesses and a lot of evidence,\" Black said.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>The club is shuttering its doors and the manager relinquished his liquor permit Monday. On Tuesday night, police released data <a href=\"/story/news/2017/03/28/logs-shed-light-police-calls-cameo-nightclub/99728580/\">pertaining to police calls for service to Kellogg Avenue club</a>.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><em>Enquirer reporter Anne Saker contributed to this report.</em></p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start Mark Wert 13 of 13 Last VideoNext Video 911 calls from the Cameo nightclub shootings\n\nPrayer vigil for the victims of the Cameo night club shooting\n\nSorting Cameo chaos, firefighter 'has job to do'\n\nCPD chief on Cameo shooting, 'The investigation is progressing'\n\nUpdate and Q&A with Enquirer reporter Sharon Coolidge on Cameo shooting\n\nWhat we know about the Cameo nightclub shootings\n\nEnquirer reporter Sharon Coolidge talks to FOP president Dan Hils about Cameo nightclub shooting\n\nPolice chief identifies man killed in Cincinnati nightclub shooting\n\nEnquirer reporter Cameron Knight discusses the latest updates in the Cincinnati nightclub shooting\n\nCameo nightclub shooting: What you need to know\n\nUpdate from the scene of a shooting at Cameo nightclub in Linwood\n\nA witness describes the shooting at Cameo nightclub in Cincinnati\n\nHow bad was the Cameo shooting?\n\nPolice operate at a crime scene outside the Cameo Nightclub after a reported fatal shooting, Sunday, March 26, 2017, in Cincinnati. At least two people opened fire inside a crowded nightclub early Sunday morning. (AP Photo/John Minchillo) (Photo: John Minchillo, AP)\n\nThe woman isn't identified. She's yelling. There's noise in the background.\n\nIt's seconds after 20 shots, possibly more, were fired inside Cameo nightclub where she was with friends on Sunday morning. She calls 911.\n\n\"There is blood everywhere. He may not make it. Hurry up! Please. He got blood all over his body. There shouldn't be shooting at clubs. We was all just dancing, next thing you look around he's shot. Friends pick up and put him in a car... damn I don't really expect anyone to get (expletive) shot in a club.\"\n\nIt's one of 11 calls pleading for emergency assistance. Some are calm. Some carry the same theme of begging emergency workers to hurry. Some simply report there was a shooting.\n\nCincinnati police released documents and audio files Wednesday pertaining to Sunday's Cameo nightclub shooting where 17 people were shot, one fatally.\n\nAn incident report showed the victims were 14 men and three women. They range in age from 24 to 33.\n\nO'Bryan Spikes, 27, died at the scene from a single shot to the chest, according to the Hamilton County Coroner's Office.\n\nThe injured: Rodney Espy, 30, Deondre Davis, 29, Jraejah Warren, 28, Stephen Haley, 28, Rayshunda Higgins, 33, Jarrod Givens, 26, Ronald Lee, 33, Nathan McClendon, 27, Shannon Brown, 25, Jordan Harris, 24, Valor Stanley, 28, Bryant Stevenson, 28, Christopher Harris, 33, Michael Feagins Jr., 30, Khristian Howell, 25 and Regina Madaris, 33.\n\nOf the 16 survivors, all but two have been released from area hospitals. The two that remain are in critical condition at University of Cincinnati Medical Center.\n\nSixty-nine law enforcement and fire personnel responded to the Cameo scene, which began unfolding around 1:30 a.m., records show.\n\nOfficers at the scene shouted to dispatchers, \"Everything you got! Expedite. Right now! Get me cars now!\"\n\nDistrict 4 Fire Chief Marc Monahan, who coordinated the chaotic scene, told The Enquirer earlier this week the call came in that six to 10 people had been shot. It would turn out to be the worst mass shooting in the city's history.\n\nThe initial call came in at 1:29 a.m. The club stayed open until 4 a.m. Police accounts say a couple of hundred people were inside at the time.\n\nPeople jumped out windows and ditched shoes, perfume and phones in the parking lot so they could move faster or hide in the bathroom, too far from the door. Some people suffered injuries while fleeing, trampled in the madness.\n\nBy 1:31 a.m. police at the scene reported \"at least six victims.\"\n\nAt 1:45 a.m., two officers reported to dispatchers that they detained someone who was standing in the club with a gun.\n\nAt 2:12 a.m., an officer reported to a dispatcher that a gun was recovered.\n\nThere have been no arrests. Police Chief Eliot Isaac said Monday he is confident police will find the people responsible for this.\n\nIn one 911 call, a caller tells the dispatcher, \"My friend's been shot. Hurry up! Hurry up!\"\n\nThe dispatcher asks if the caller knows who shot his friend and the caller replies no. The caller can be heard asking someone if they should load the shooting victim into a vehicle.\n\n\"Do not move him. Hello? Please do not move him,\" the dispatcher says.\n\nAnother caller tells a dispatcher he has two friends shot.\n\n\"I was running for my life,\" the caller said after being asked if he saw anything.\n\nAnother person called from the bathroom.\n\n\"I'm in the bathroom and they're saying they're shooting inside and outside. And I don't know what to do, I lost my friend.\" Later, the caller asks the dispatcher, \"Is it done?\"\n\nEight minutes after the initial dispatch call, a dispatcher reported, \"Any available unit in the city is responding at this time, plus county units.\"\n\nOfficers on the scene were finding people in cars and down the road. They had been shot but fled.\n\nOne man was found shot under the entrance awning. Two others in a car. One man who had been shot in the head was picked up by an ambulance at near Stanley Avenue.\n\nTwelve minutes after the initial dispatch another victim was located in the nightclub's parking lot.\n\nSome victims drove themselves to the hospital.\n\nAccording to dispatch traffic, by 1:49 a.m. two shooting victims had walked into University of Cincinnati Medical Center. Twenty minutes later two \"walk-in\" shooting victims arrived at Bethesda North Hospital. More than 45 minutes after the initial call, another victim walked into the Short Vine fire station.\n\nCincinnati City Manager Harry Black told city council Wednesday that police officers investigating the Cameo nightclub shootings are \"making substantial and significant progress.\"\n\nBut, he urged patience.\n\n\"There are a lot of witnesses and a lot of evidence,\" Black said.\n\nThe club is shuttering its doors and the manager relinquished his liquor permit Monday. On Tuesday night, police released data pertaining to police calls for service to Kellogg Avenue club.\n\nEnquirer reporter Anne Saker contributed to this report.\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\nRead or Share this story: http://cin.ci/2nBqpHD", "images":
